00047|         let owner = self.runtime.authenticated_signer()
00048|             .expect("Operation must be signed")
00049|             .to_string();
00050|         
00051|         let current_chain = self.runtime.chain_id();
00052|         let registry_chain_id = self.state.registry_chain_id.get()
00053|             .expect("Registry chain ID not set");
00054| 
00055|         match operation {
00056|             Operation::Register { name } => {
00057|                 // Validate domain name
00058|                 assert!(!name.is_empty(), "Domain name cannot be empty");
00059|                 assert!(name.len() <= 63, "Domain name too long");
00060|                 assert!(
00061|                     name.chars().all(|c| c.is_ascii_alphanumeric() || c == '-'),
00062|                     "Invalid characters in domain name"
00063|                 );
00064| 
00065|                 if current_chain == registry_chain_id {
00066|                     // We ARE the registry chain - register directly
00067|                     let existing = self.state.domains.get(&name).await.expect("Failed to read state");
00068|                     assert!(existing.is_none(), "Domain already registered");
00069|                     self.state.domains.insert(&name, owner).expect("Failed to register domain");
00070|                 } else {
00071|                     // Send registration request to registry chain
00072|                     let message = Message::RequestRegister {
00073|                         name,
00074|                         owner,
00075|                         requester_chain: current_chain,
00076|                     };
00077|                     self.runtime.send_message(registry_chain_id, message);
00078|                 }
00079|             }
00080|             Operation::Transfer { name, new_owner } => {
00081|                 if current_chain == registry_chain_id {
00082|                     // We ARE the registry chain - transfer directly
00083|                     let current_owner = self.state.domains.get(&name).await
00084|                         .expect("Failed to read state")
00085|                         .expect("Domain not registered");
00086|                     assert_eq!(current_owner, owner, "Not the domain owner");
00087|                     self.state.domains.insert(&name, new_owner).expect("Failed to transfer domain");
00088|                 } else {
00089|                     // Send transfer request to registry chain
00090|                     let message = Message::RequestTransfer {
00091|                         name,
00092|                         new_owner,
00093|                         current_owner: owner,
00094|                         requester_chain: current_chain,
00095|                     };
00096|                     self.runtime.send_message(registry_chain_id, message);
00097|                 }
00098|             }
00099|         }
00100|     }
00101| 
00102|     async fn execute_message(&mut self, message: Self::Message) {
00103|         let current_chain = self.runtime.chain_id();
00104|         let registry_chain_id = self.state.registry_chain_id.get()
00105|             .expect("Registry chain ID not set");
00106| 
00107|         match message {
00108|             Message::RequestRegister { name, owner, requester_chain } => {
00109|                 // Only the registry chain should process registration requests
00110|                 assert_eq!(current_chain, registry_chain_id, "Only registry chain can process registrations");
00111|                 
00112|                 let existing = self.state.domains.get(&name).await.expect("Failed to read state");
00113|                 if existing.is_some() {
00114|                     // Domain already taken - send failure response
00115|                     let response = Message::RegistrationFailed {
00116|                         name,
00117|                         reason: "Domain already registered".to_string(),
00118|                     };
00119|                     self.runtime.send_message(requester_chain, response);
00120|                 } else {
00121|                     // Register the domain
00122|                     self.state.domains.insert(&name, owner).expect("Failed to register domain");
00123|                     let response = Message::RegistrationSuccess { name };
00124|                     self.runtime.send_message(requester_chain, response);
00125|                 }
00126|             }
00127|             Message::RequestTransfer { name, new_owner, current_owner, requester_chain } => {
00128|                 // Only the registry chain should process transfer requests
00129|                 assert_eq!(current_chain, registry_chain_id, "Only registry chain can process transfers");
00130|                 
00131|                 let stored_owner = self.state.domains.get(&name).await.expect("Failed to read state");
00132|                 match stored_owner {
00133|                     None => {
00134|                         let response = Message::TransferFailed {
00135|                             name,
00136|                             reason: "Domain not registered".to_string(),
00137|                         };
00138|                         self.runtime.send_message(requester_chain, response);
00139|                     }
00140|                     Some(owner) if owner != current_owner => {
00141|                         let response = Message::TransferFailed {
00142|                             name,
00143|                             reason: "Not the domain owner".to_string(),
00144|                         };
00145|                         self.runtime.send_message(requester_chain, response);
00146|                     }
00147|                     Some(_) => {
00148|                         // Transfer ownership
00149|                         self.state.domains.insert(&name, new_owner.clone()).expect("Failed to transfer domain");
00150|                         let response = Message::TransferSuccess { name, new_owner };
00151|                         self.runtime.send_message(requester_chain, response);
00152|                     }
00153|                 }
00154|             }
00155|             Message::RegistrationSuccess { name } => {
00156|                 // Received confirmation that registration succeeded
00157|                 // Could emit an event or update local cache here
00158|                 let _ = name; // Acknowledge receipt
00159|             }
00160|             Message::RegistrationFailed { name, reason } => {
00161|                 // Registration failed
00162|                 let _ = (name, reason); // Acknowledge receipt
00163|             }
00164|             Message::TransferSuccess { name, new_owner } => {
00165|                 // Transfer succeeded
00166|                 let _ = (name, new_owner); // Acknowledge receipt
00167|             }
00168|             Message::TransferFailed { name, reason } => {
00169|                 // Transfer failed
00170|                 let _ = (name, reason); // Acknowledge receipt
00171|             }
00172|         }
00173|     }

00176|         self.state.save().await.expect("Failed to save state");
00177|     }

## Assistant

The issue is that when a user's chain runs the contract, the `registry_chain_id` is `None` because `instantiate()` only runs on the deploying chain. We need to use the application's creation chain ID instead, which is available via `runtime.application_id().creation.chain_id`.

**Tool Call: contracts/linera_name_system/src/contract.rs**
Status: Completed



Diff: [PROJECT_ROOT]/linera-name-system/contracts/linera_name_system/src/contract.rs
```
#![cfg_attr(target_arch = "wasm32", no_main)]

mod state;

use linera_sdk::{
    abi::WithContractAbi,
    views::{RootView, View},
    Contract, ContractRuntime,
};

use linera_name_system::{Message, Operation};
use self::state::LineraNameSystemState;

pub struct LineraNameSystemContract {
    state: LineraNameSystemState,
    runtime: ContractRuntime<Self>,
}

linera_sdk::contract!(LineraNameSystemContract);

impl WithContractAbi for LineraNameSystemContract {
    type Abi = linera_name_system::LineraNameSystemAbi;
}

impl LineraNameSystemContract {
    /// Get the registry chain ID - this is always the chain where the application was created
    fn registry_chain_id(&self) -> linera_sdk::linera_base_types::ChainId {
        self.runtime.application_id().creation.chain_id
    }
}

impl Contract for LineraNameSystemContract {
    type Message = Message;
    type Parameters = ();
    type InstantiationArgument = ();
    type EventValue = ();

    async fn load(runtime: ContractRuntime<Self>) -> Self {
        let state = LineraNameSystemState::load(runtime.root_view_storage_context())
            .await
            .expect("Failed to load state");
        LineraNameSystemContract { state, runtime }
    }

    async fn instantiate(&mut self, _argument: Self::InstantiationArgument) {
        // Nothing to initialize - registry chain is derived from application_id
    }

    async fn execute_operation(&mut self, operation: Self::Operation) -> Self::Response {
        let owner = self.runtime.authenticated_signer()
            .expect("Operation must be signed")
            .to_string();
        
        let current_chain = self.runtime.chain_id();
        let registry_chain_id = self.registry_chain_id();

        match operation {
            Operation::Register { name } => {
                // Validate domain name
                assert!(!name.is_empty(), "Domain name cannot be empty");
                assert!(name.len() <= 63, "Domain name too long");
                assert!(
                    name.chars().all(|c| c.is_ascii_alphanumeric() || c == '-'),
                    "Invalid characters in domain name"
                );

                if current_chain == registry_chain_id {
                    // We ARE the registry chain - register directly
                    let existing = self.state.domains.get(&name).await.expect("Failed to read state");
                    assert!(existing.is_none(), "Domain already registered");
                    self.state.domains.insert(&name, owner).expect("Failed to register domain");
                } else {
                    // Send registration request to registry chain
                    let message = Message::RequestRegister {
                        name,
                        owner,
                        requester_chain: current_chain,
                    };
                    self.runtime.send_message(registry_chain_id, message);
                }
            }
            Operation::Transfer { name, new_owner } => {
                if current_chain == registry_chain_id {
                    // We ARE the registry chain - transfer directly
                    let current_owner = self.state.domains.get(&name).await
                        .expect("Failed to read state")
                        .expect("Domain not registered");
                    assert_eq!(current_owner, owner, "Not the domain owner");
                    self.state.domains.insert(&name, new_owner).expect("Failed to transfer domain");
                } else {
                    // Send transfer request to registry chain
                    let message = Message::RequestTransfer {
                        name,
                        new_owner,
                        current_owner: owner,
                        requester_chain: current_chain,
                    };
                    self.runtime.send_message(registry_chain_id, message);
                }
            }
        }
    }

    async fn execute_message(&mut self, message: Self::Message) {
        let current_chain = self.runtime.chain_id();
        let registry_chain_id = self.registry_chain_id();

        match message {
            Message::RequestRegister { name, owner, requester_chain } => {
                // Only the registry chain should process registration requests
                assert_eq!(current_chain, registry_chain_id, "Only registry chain can process registrations");
                
                let existing = self.state.domains.get(&name).await.expect("Failed to read state");
                if existing.is_some() {
                    // Domain already taken - send failure response
                    let response = Message::RegistrationFailed {
                        name,
                        reason: "Domain already registered".to_string(),
                    };
                    self.runtime.send_message(requester_chain, response);
                } else {
                    // Register the domain
                    self.state.domains.insert(&name, owner).expect("Failed to register domain");
                    let response = Message::RegistrationSuccess { name };
                    self.runtime.send_message(requester_chain, response);
                }
            }
            Message::RequestTransfer { name, new_owner, current_owner, requester_chain } => {
                // Only the registry chain should process transfer requests
                assert_eq!(current_chain, registry_chain_id, "Only registry chain can process transfers");
                
                let stored_owner = self.state.domains.get(&name).await.expect("Failed to read state");
                match stored_owner {
                    None => {
                        let response = Message::TransferFailed {
                            name,
                            reason: "Domain not registered".to_string(),
                        };
                        self.runtime.send_message(requester_chain, response);
                    }
                    Some(owner) if owner != current_owner => {
                        let response = Message::TransferFailed {
                            name,
                            reason: "Not the domain owner".to_string(),
                        };
                        self.runtime.send_message(requester_chain, response);
                    }
                    Some(_) => {
                        // Transfer ownership
                        self.state.domains.insert(&name, new_owner.clone()).expect("Failed to transfer domain");
                        let response = Message::TransferSuccess { name, new_owner };
                        self.runtime.send_message(requester_chain, response);
                    }
                }
            }
            Message::RegistrationSuccess { name } => {
                // Received confirmation that registration succeeded
                let _ = name;
            }
            Message::RegistrationFailed { name, reason } => {
                // Registration failed
                let _ = (name, reason);
            }
            Message::TransferSuccess { name, new_owner } => {
                // Transfer succeeded
                let _ = (name, new_owner);
            }
            Message::TransferFailed { name, reason } => {
                // Transfer failed
                let _ = (name, reason);
            }
        }
    }

    async fn store(mut self) {
        self.state.save().await.expect("Failed to save state");
    }
}
```

```
#![cfg_attr(target_arch = "wasm32", no_main)]

mod state;

use async_graphql::{EmptySubscription, Object, Request, Response, Schema};
use linera_sdk::{
    abi::WithServiceAbi,
    views::View,
    Service, ServiceRuntime,
};
use std::sync::Arc;

use linera_name_system::Operation;
use self::state::LineraNameSystemState;

pub struct LineraNameSystemService {
    state: Arc<LineraNameSystemState>,
    runtime: Arc<ServiceRuntime<Self>>,
}

linera_sdk::service!(LineraNameSystemService);

impl WithServiceAbi for LineraNameSystemService {
    type Abi = linera_name_system::LineraNameSystemAbi;
}

impl Service for LineraNameSystemService {
    type Parameters = ();

    async fn new(runtime: ServiceRuntime<Self>) -> Self {
        let state = LineraNameSystemState::load(runtime.root_view_storage_context())
            .await
            .expect("Failed to load state");
        LineraNameSystemService { 
            state: Arc::new(state),
            runtime: Arc::new(runtime),
        }
    }

    async fn handle_query(&self, request: Request) -> Response {
        let schema = Schema::build(QueryRoot, MutationRoot, EmptySubscription)
            .data(self.state.clone())
            .data(self.runtime.clone())
            .finish();
        schema.execute(request).await
    }
}

struct QueryRoot;

#[Object]
impl QueryRoot {
    /// Look up the owner of a domain
    async fn owner(&self, ctx: &async_graphql::Context<'_>, name: String) -> Option<String> {
        let state = ctx.data_unchecked::<Arc<LineraNameSystemState>>();
        state.domains.get(&name).await.ok().flatten()
    }

    /// Check if a domain is available
    async fn is_available(&self, ctx: &async_graphql::Context<'_>, name: String) -> bool {
        let state = ctx.data_unchecked::<Arc<LineraNameSystemState>>();
        state.domains.get(&name).await.ok().flatten().is_none()
    }

    /// Get the registry chain ID (the source of truth for all domains)
    async fn registry_chain_id(&self, ctx: &async_graphql::Context<'_>) -> String {
        let runtime = ctx.data_unchecked::<Arc<ServiceRuntime<LineraNameSystemService>>>();
        runtime.application_id().creation.chain_id.to_string()
    }

    /// List all registered domains (only accurate on registry chain)
    async fn all_domains(&self, ctx: &async_graphql::Context<'_>) -> Vec<DomainInfo> {
        let state = ctx.data_unchecked::<Arc<LineraNameSystemState>>();
        let mut domains = Vec::new();
        let _ = state.domains.for_each_index_value(|name, owner| {
            domains.push(DomainInfo {
                name: name.clone(),
                owner: owner.to_string(),
            });
            Ok(())
        }).await;
        domains
    }
}

#[derive(async_graphql::SimpleObject)]
struct DomainInfo {
    name: String,
    owner: String,
}

struct MutationRoot;

#[Object]
impl MutationRoot {
    /// Register a new .linera domain
    async fn register(&self, ctx: &async_graphql::Context<'_>, name: String) -> bool {
        let runtime = ctx.data_unchecked::<Arc<ServiceRuntime<LineraNameSystemService>>>();
        let operation = Operation::Register { name };
        runtime.schedule_operation(&operation);
        true
    }

    /// Transfer domain ownership
    async fn transfer(&self, ctx: &async_graphql::Context<'_>, name: String, new_owner: String) -> bool {
        let runtime = ctx.data_unchecked::<Arc<ServiceRuntime<LineraNameSystemService>>>();
        let operation = Operation::Transfer { name, new_owner };
        runtime.schedule_operation(&operation);
        true
    }
}
```

**Tool Call: **
Status: Completed

You are asking how to retrieve the chain ID where an application was created or deployed, given an `ApplicationId`, from within a contract or service. You also want to know the fields available on `ApplicationId` .

### Accessing the Creator Chain ID

Within a contract or service, you can access the creator chain ID using the `application_creator_chain_id()` method provided by the runtime.

For Rust-based contracts and services, the `linera-sdk` provides `ContractRuntime` and `ServiceRuntime` structs, respectively, which expose this functionality  . These runtimes internally call `base_wit::get_application_creator_chain_id()`  , which is part of the WebAssembly Interface Types (WIT) bindings. The WIT binding `get_application_creator_chain_id` is implemented by `BaseRuntimeApi::get_application_creator_chain_id` , which in turn calls the `application_creator_chain_id()` method on the underlying `BaseRuntime` implementation .

The `application_creator_chain_id()` method in the `SyncRuntimeInternal` (which implements `BaseRuntime`) retrieves this information from the `description` field of the currently executing application .

For Solidity contracts, the `Linera.sol` library provides a function `application_creator_chain_id()` that interacts with a precompile to get this value . This precompile corresponds to `BaseRuntimePrecompile::ApplicationCreatorChainId` .

### Fields of `ApplicationId`

The `ApplicationId` is derived from an `ApplicationDescription` . The `ApplicationDescription` struct contains the following fields :
*   `module_id`: The unique ID of the bytecode used for the application .
*   `creator_chain_id`: The `ChainId` that created the application . This is the field you are looking for.
*   `block_height`: The height of the block that created this application .
*   `application_index`: The index of the application among those created in the same block .
*   `parameters`: The parameters of the application .
*   `required_application_ids`: Required dependencies of the application .

The `ApplicationId` itself is a `CryptoHash` of the `ApplicationDescription` . Therefore, to get the `creator_chain_id` from an `ApplicationId`, you would typically need to retrieve the full `ApplicationDescription` that the `ApplicationId` refers to. However, as shown above, the runtime provides a direct way to access the `creator_chain_id` of the *current* application without needing to reconstruct the `ApplicationDescription` from the `ApplicationId` .

## Notes

The `ApplicationId` in Solidity is represented as a struct containing a `CryptoHash` . The `BaseRuntimePrecompile` enum also includes variants for other runtime functionalities like `ChainId`, `BlockHeight`, `ReadSystemTimestamp`, and `ReadChainBalance` .

Wiki pages you might want to explore:
- [Execution System (linera-io/linera-protocol)](/wiki/linera-io/linera-protocol#4)

View this search on DeepWiki: https://deepwiki.com/search/how-can-i-get-the-chain-id-whe_5e2d4a74-fdd8-4c16-b1cc-08d6bc940572

## Assistant

The fix has been deployed. Here's a summary of what was changed:

## Fix Summary

**Problem:** The contract was panicking because `registry_chain_id` was stored in state and only set during `instantiate()` on the deploying chain. When users connected from their own chains, the state was empty, causing `expect("Registry chain ID not set")` to panic.

**Solution:** Instead of storing the registry chain ID in state, we now derive it dynamically using `runtime.application_creator_chain_id()`. This method returns the chain ID where the application was originally created/deployed, which is available on ALL chains running the application.

### Changes Made:

1. **`contract.rs`** - Added helper method that uses `application_creator_chain_id()`:
   ```rust
   fn registry_chain_id(&mut self) -> ChainId {
       self.runtime.application_creator_chain_id()
   }
   ```

2. **`service.rs`** - Updated `registryChainId` query to use the same approach:
   ```rust
   runtime.application_creator_chain_id().to_string()
   ```

3. **`state.rs`** - Removed the `registry_chain_id` field since it's no longer needed in state.

### New Application ID
```
b029509660d95226224ba0a6d6fc33cd4c341b29654ecf084699ee14588a16dd
```

### Registry Chain ID
```
165f2f8a389e61d870d0afa52803643df413e4d085aef63666bd8fd9fce4ffcc
```

Now when a user connects from their own chain and tries to register a domain:
1. The contract gets the registry chain ID via `application_creator_chain_id()`
2. Since the user's chain != registry chain, it sends a cross-chain message to the registry
3. The registry chain processes the registration and sends back a confirmation

Restart your dev server and try registering a domain again.

## Assistant

I can see the issue now. After registering "testdomain123", when I click "Check Availability" again, it shows "Available!" instead of "Already registered". This confirms the problem - the frontend is querying the **user's chain** (which has empty local state) instead of the **registry chain** (which has the actual domain data).

Let me check the console for more details and understand the issue better.
